## Blasts from the past: New insights from old space storms
 - [https://phys.org/news/2024-10-blasts-insights-space-storms.html](https://phys.org/news/2024-10-blasts-insights-space-storms.html)
 - RSS feed: $source
 - date published: 2024-10-25T01:03:15.261319+00:00

On 4 August 1972, a burst of solar plasma rocked Earth's magnetic field after hurtling through space for about 14.6 hours—the fastest sun-to-Earth plasma journey ever recorded. The resulting space storm, one of several that occurred from 2 to 11 August, triggered widespread disturbances to electrical and communication grids and likely caused accidental detonations of U.S. undersea naval mines in North Vietnam.

Bacteria evolve rapidly in the human gut by sharing genetic elements with each other. Bacteriodales is a prolific order of gut bacteria that trade hundreds of genetic elements. Little is known, however, about the effects of these DNA transfers, either to the fitness of the bacteria or the host.

 - [https://phys.org/news/2024-10-invasive-silver-carp-movement-chicago.html](https://phys.org/news/2024-10-invasive-silver-carp-movement-chicago.html)
 - RSS feed: $source
 - date published: 2024-10-25T09:59:16.347971+00:00

Invasive silver carp have been spreading throughout the Mississippi River Basin since their introduction a half-century ago. Yet, try as they might, the fish have not advanced beyond a particular stretch of the Illinois River north of Kankakee. ## Saturn's moon Titan has insulating methane-rich crust up to six miles thick
 - [https://phys.org/news/2024-10-saturn-moon-titan-insulating-methane.html](https://phys.org/news/2024-10-saturn-moon-titan-insulating-methane.html)

Saturn's largest moon, Titan, is the only place other than Earth known to have an atmosphere and liquids in the form of rivers, lakes and seas on its surface.
